Recently I have received a lot of queries regarding my preparation that landed me in FAANG/MAANG companies. Below are some of the resources that helped me a lot \-

✅ 𝐂𝐨𝐝𝐢𝐧𝐠 𝐈𝐧𝐭𝐞𝐫𝐯𝐢𝐞𝐰  
👉 Solve LeetCode medium-level problems (at least more than 250+ covering different topics)  
👉 I have created an xlsx on top/important 500 leetCode questions (https://lnkd.in/dWn73jXd) and a video on How to Crack The Coding Interview (https://lnkd.in/dsn4cipq)  
👉 Clement Mihailescu's \- https://www.algoexpert.io/ 200+ handpicked questions (In case you want to prepare fast and only good questions)  
👉 I watched my DSA playlist to revise concepts at 2x speed (https://lnkd.in/dJfS9FkD)  
👉 Grokking the Coding Interview (https://lnkd.in/dfKHYUQK) \- It has covered various coding problems segregated based on coding patterns

✅ 𝐒𝐲𝐬𝐭𝐞𝐦 𝐃𝐞𝐬𝐢𝐠𝐧 𝐈𝐧𝐭𝐞𝐫𝐯𝐢𝐞𝐰  
👉 Arslan Ahmad's Grokking the System Design Interview \- It has step-by-step discussion and good case studies on system design (https://lnkd.in/dXywra2R)  
👉 Alex Xu's System Design Interview course on ByteByteGo (https://lnkd.in/d6yRpRvy) \- It covers all the content from his famous book (Vol 1 & Vol 2\) System Design Interview  
👉 \#SystemsExpert (https://lnkd.in/d-5mSpfw) videos to know how real-life System Design Interviews go

✅ 𝐋𝐨𝐰-𝐋𝐞𝐯𝐞𝐥 𝐃𝐞𝐬𝐢𝐠𝐧 𝐈𝐧𝐭𝐞𝐫𝐯𝐢𝐞𝐰  
👉 Grokking the Object Oriented Design Interview (https://lnkd.in/deuAXR-U) \- A very detailed & step-by-step approach to various OOD case studies   
👉 Try practicing drawing UML diagrams on Diagrams.net

✅ 𝐀𝐏𝐈 𝐃𝐞𝐬𝐢𝐠𝐧 𝐈𝐧𝐭𝐞𝐫𝐯𝐢𝐞𝐰  
👉 Best Practices (https://lnkd.in/d\_x39xkK), Implementation (https://lnkd.in/d5fhXZJ7), & Guidelines (https://lnkd.in/dr397Hy2) of API Design  
👉 Look for use cases like \- Stripe (https://lnkd.in/dsM7PpJt) & Twitter (https://lnkd.in/dxiMu8wr) API Documentation  
👉 Follow https://lnkd.in/dA5AUaz3\#/ to understand how APIs should be designed

✅ 𝐃𝐚𝐭𝐚𝐛𝐚𝐬𝐞 𝐃𝐞𝐬𝐢𝐠𝐧 𝐈𝐧𝐭𝐞𝐫𝐯𝐢𝐞𝐰  
👉 Grokking the Object Oriented Design Interview (https://lnkd.in/deuAXR-U) \- Take the case studies and try to apply Object to Relational Mapping strategy  
👉 Try practicing drawing relational schema on https://drawsql.app

✅ 𝐁𝐞𝐡𝐚𝐯𝐢𝐨𝐫𝐚𝐥 𝐈𝐧𝐭𝐞𝐫𝐯𝐢𝐞𝐰

2yr •   
2yr Visible to everyone

𝗜 𝗵𝗮𝘃𝗲 𝘁𝗮𝗸𝗲𝗻 𝟱𝟬+ 𝗶𝗻𝘁𝗲𝗿𝘃𝗶𝗲𝘄𝘀 𝗮𝘁 𝗚𝗼𝗼𝗴𝗹𝗲.  
From my personal experience, major things many folks can improve about how to approach an interview \- 

● When the interviewer is explaining the problem, listen carefully. Ask for clarifications if there is any doubt in the problem statement.   
It's fine to take 1-2 extra minutes in this step. As if you understand the problem incorrectly, then you would waste many more extra minutes.  
Also sometimes it's possible that the problem asked is different from a very common standard problem in a nuanced way, if you try to hurry too much in such cases you can mistake the problem for the standard version.  
   
● After listening to the problem statement, think through it from all angles for a couple of minutes. You don't have to speak the first thing that comes to your mind (balance is tricky for this, as I will also add in the next point).  
Take a couple of minutes to see if there are any non-obvious things that didn't strike you the first time.  
   
● The tricky thing with the previous point is that there should be a balance. If you have thought for let's say 5-7 minutes and any solution better than the straightforward brute force solution is not coming to your mind, then you should convey that solution to the interviewer.  
One because time is limited during the interview, you shouldn't keep thinking indefinitely.  
Secondly sometimes when you reach a dead end in thinking, then just explaining your current version can help you progress further. Also, the interviewer has the chance to ask questions that can help you in improving the current solution.  
   
● Explaining why your proposed solution is correct is as important as (maybe more) telling the correct solution. Many folks underestimate it, they think that it's all about telling the correct solution. But explaining it is very important because that tells the interviewer about how you think and also that you actually understand the problem being discussed here.  
Additionally, arguably this is one of the skills which is directly applicable to software developer roles. How you approach a problem is very important because, unlike algorithmic interviews in actual development, you will often face open-ended situations, where your way of approaching will matter the most.  
   
● Thinking through the edge cases. After you are done coding your solution, take a couple of examples to dry run through your code, you can also walk the interviewer through your code during this process. If your code is working correctly on the examples you tried, then try to think of any possible edge cases your code may suffer from.  
   
If you found this useful, like this post to encourage me to write more such posts.

Disclaimer \- All opinions expressed here are solely personal.

\#interviewpreparation \#interviewprep \#google  
\#datastructures \#algorithms \#interviewskills  
…see more

\=== POST 109 \===  
Prakash Tiwari  
View Prakash Tiwari’s profile  
   
• 2nd  
VP- Lead Software Engineer |AI enthusiast|Senior Principal Software Engineer(Architect)|.Net, Azure|System Design|Technical Architect-Hands on (Azure Cloud Certified)|Learner| Cloud Practitioner|LLD and HLD|DSA|

2yr •   
2yr Visible to everyone

While watching the podcast by Arpit Bhayani with Saurabh, there was a brief discussion on Anycast architecture, which is incorporated in the Dukaan design to attain low latency and high availability. Its simple but powerful.  
Anycast or IP Anycast: The architecture which underpins the 100% uptime SLA and high performance, low latency.  
Multiple cloud nodes or instances of a service{deployed in the different datacenter} announce/advertise and share the same publicly accessible IP address. So for example, the IP address of 11.12.13.14 would be advertised for the cloud node in Singapore at the same time as it is being advertised for the node in London, New York, India and others.

Anycast is similar to Multicast, except that the client connects to a single node, even though multiple nodes may advertise their availability to deliver the service. However, it is important to note that the client may not know of multiple nodes and assume there is only one, which is by design.  
Note: It works only in stateless design configuration. Content synchronization becomes the cardinal engineering concern.

Following are the badvantages of using the Anycast:  
Increased Reliability: Reliability of a network-based service is enhanced by the placement of multiple, geographically dispersed servers or clusters using the same IP address. In the event one server or server cluster fails, traffic is simply redirected to another node without having to change IP addresses.  
Load Balancing: Nicely load balances traffic over different nodes based on geography of the client.  
Increased Performance: Traffic destined for an Anycast node will be routed to the topologically nearest node to the client, thus reducing latency between the client and the node.  
Attack Mitigation: Geographically dispersed server clusters operating using the same publicly announced IP address naturally attract attacks to them, thus sinking the attack requests closer to the origin.  
Enhanced Availability: In the event that an Anycast node becomes unavailable, traffic can simply shift to an alternate node as soon as the routes are withdrawn from the routing table without the need for the client to communicate with a new IP address.  
Moreover anycast is beneficial in case of migrating to the different cloud vendor, without changing the clients consuming the hosted services.

\=== POST 111 \===  
Nachiket Kanore  
View Nachiket Kanore’s profile  
   
• 1st  
Software Development Engineer 2 @Amazon | Ex-PhonePe | Backend Engineer | AI & LLMs

2yr •   
2yr Visible to everyone

■ 𝗧𝗵𝗲 𝗟𝗮𝗿𝗴𝗲𝘀𝘁 𝗗𝗗𝗼𝗦 𝗮𝘁𝘁𝗮𝗰𝗸 𝘁𝗼 𝗱𝗮𝘁𝗲 𝗼𝗻 𝗚𝗼𝗼𝗴𝗹𝗲:

✔ The recent DDoS attacks on multiple Google infrastructures reached a peak of 398 million requests per second (rps) and relied on a novel HTTP/2 “Rapid Reset” technique based on stream multiplexing.

✔ For a sense of scale, this two-minute attack generated more requests than the total number of article views reported by Wikipedia during the entire month of September 2023\.

■ 𝗪𝗵𝗮𝘁 𝗶𝘀 𝗛𝗧𝗧𝗣/𝟮 𝘀𝘁𝗿𝗲𝗮𝗺 𝗺𝘂𝗹𝘁𝗶𝗽𝗹𝗲𝘅𝗶𝗻𝗴?

✔ With HTTP/2, the client can open multiple concurrent streams on a single TCP connection, each stream corresponding to one HTTP request. The maximum number of concurrent open streams is, in theory, controllable by the server, but in practice, clients may open 100 streams per request and the servers process these requests in parallel.

✔ For example, the client can open 100 streams and send a request on each of them in a single round trip; the proxy will read and process each stream serially, but the requests to the backend servers can again be parallelized. 

■ 𝗪𝗵𝗮𝘁 𝗶𝘀 𝘁𝗵𝗲 𝗛𝗧𝗧𝗣/𝟮, 𝗥𝗮𝗽𝗶𝗱 𝗥𝗲𝘀𝗲𝘁’ 𝗗𝗗𝗼𝗦 𝗮𝘁𝘁𝗮𝗰𝗸?

✔ The client can then open new streams as it receives responses to the previous ones. This gives an effective throughput for a single connection of 100 requests per round trip, with similar round trip timing constants to HTTP/1.1 requests. This will typically lead to almost 100 times higher utilization of each connection.

✔ The HTTP/2 protocol allows clients to indicate to the server that a previous stream should be canceled by sending an RST\_STREAM frame. The protocol does not require the client and server to coordinate the cancellation in any way, the client may do it unilaterally. The client may also assume that the cancellation will take effect immediately when the server receives the RST\_STREAM frame, before any other data from that TCP connection is processed.

✔ The client opens a large number of streams at once as in the standard HTTP/2 attack, but rather than waiting for a response to each request stream from the server or proxy, the client cancels each request immediately.

✔ The ability to reset streams immediately allows each connection to have an indefinite number of requests in flight. By explicitly canceling the requests, the attacker never exceeds the limit on the number of concurrent open streams

✔ In a typical HTTP/2 server implementation, the server will still have to do significant amounts of work for canceled requests, such as allocating new stream data structures, parsing the query and doing header decompression, and mapping the URL to a resource.

Refer to the following diagrams for comparisons between the attacks\!

Dipanshu Pandey

2yr •   
2yr Visible to everyone

Hey everyone,

I'm thrilled to share that I secured the 2nd position worldwide and 1st in India in today's BiWeekly contest\! 

Here's a quick rundown of how I solved the problems:

1: For the first problem, I found a neat trick \- iterating in reverse order and using sets or maps in C++ to quickly locate the first index where all values from 1 to K are encountered.

2: Problem 2 was all about counting the frequency of values. If there was an element with a frequency of 1, it posed a challenge as we couldn't remove it. Otherwise, I simply added frq\[element\]/3, incrementing if there was a remainder after the division.

3: The key insight for problem 3 was recognizing that we could only have one partition if the total AND of the array was greater than 0\. The rest was just finding a subarray with 0 AND.

4: Lastly, for problem 4, I focused on subtrees with sums divisible by K since the overall sum had to be divisible by K. This greedy approach helped maximize the partition.

I also want to take a moment to express my gratitude to Rangey Raghav, who previously secured Global rank 1 position and motivated me for this performance. Guess what? I beat him in this contest Haha\!

Unlocking the Power of Learning: My Top 10 Resources for Software engineering Realm\! 🚀📚

An indie hacker just created the most useful GPT-4 prompt ever written. You can use it to you help make engineering decisions in unfamiliar territory:

"""  
You are an engineering wizard, experienced at solving complex problems across various disciplines. Your knowledge is both wide and deep. You are also a great communicator, giving very thoughtful and clear advice.

You do so in this format, thinking through the challenges you are facing, then proposing multiple solutions, then reviewing each solution, looking for issues or possible improvements, coming up with a possible new and better solution (you can combine ideas from the other solutions, bring in new ideas, etc.), then giving a final recommendation:

\`\`\`  
\#\# Problem Overview  
$problem\_overview

\#\# Challenges  
$challenges

\#\# Solution 1  
$solution\_1

\#\# Solution 2  
$solution\_2

\#\# Solution 3  
$solution\_3

\#\# Analysis

\#\#\# Solution 1 Analysis  
$solution\_1\_analysis

\#\#\# Solution 2 Analysis  
$solution\_2\_analysis

\#\#\# Solution 3 Analysis  
$solution\_3\_analysis

\#\# Additional Possible Solution  
$additional\_possible\_solution

\#\# Recommendation  
$recommendation  
\`\`\`

Each section (Problem Overview, Challenges, Solution 1, Solution 2, Solution 3, Solution 1 Analysis, Solution 2 Analysis, Solution 3 Analysis, Additional Possible Solution, and Recommendation) should be incredibly thoughtful, comprising at a minimum, four sentences of thinking.

ChatGPT is the biggest career hack available right now.

Use it to transform your thinking capacity. 

6 mental models and how you can use them with ChatGPT:

1\. Occam’s Razor

Prompt: “I have two potential plans. I want to use the Occam's Razor framework to find the solution which relies on the fewest assumptions and complexities. Option 1 involves \[provide details of the first option\], and Option 2 involves \[provide details of the second option\]. Suggest the most straightforward option.”

2\. Cost-Benefit Analysis

Prompt: "Act like a business analyst. Use the Cost-Benefit Analysis framework to evaluate whether \[insert decision\] is a net benefit or a net loss given \[insert constraints & limitations\]. Suggest any resources that could be used to deal with the costs and identify potential risks & benefits.”

3\. The Eisenhower Matrix

Prompt: " I am a \[insert job title\]. Here is a list of activities I have for this week. 

\[insert list\]

"Help me prioritize my tasks in terms of importance and urgency using the Eisenhower matrix."

4\. Social Proof

Prompt: “Act like a Content Marketer. Suggest ways in which I can incorporate social proof into my content in order to increase trust and credibility with my readers?"

5\. Network Effects

Prompt: “Act as a Product Manager. Analyze \[insert business decision\] through the understanding of Network Effects. Consider how the value of a product, which has the following features increases as more people use it:

\[insert list of features\]”

6\. Risk-reward analysis:

Prompt: "Act like a Growth Analyst. Use the Risk-Reward framework to identify the risk and rewards associated with \[insert strategy\]. Suggest the implementation plan for each strategy as well as the steps that can be taken to reduce risk."

\=== POST 125 \===  
Arpit Bhayani  
View Arpit Bhayani’s profile  
   
• 2nd  
Principal Engineer II at Razorpay • databases • ex-Staff Engineer at GCP Memorystore and GCP Dataproc • creator of DiceDB • built and sold Profile.fyi • ex-Amazon Fast Data and DoE Unacademy

2yr •   
2yr Visible to everyone

Projects are the best way to learn a programming language, and here are the three projects that I did learn Golang back in 2016 ⚡

1\. Build a command-line todo application  
2\. Build a simple in-memory message broker  
3\. Chat Application using WebSockets

Each project covers a different aspect of Golang and doing them all builds a holistic understanding. Here's what you will get from each project.

1\. Build a command-line todo application

Golang is heavily used to build internal tools and command-line utilities. Building a todo application on CLI will help you

\- start with Go without being intimidated by the problem statement  
\- understand how to structure the code and follow best practices

2\. Build a simple in-memory message broker

Message brokers are simple queues exposed over the network. Doing this project will help you understand

\- writing HTTP web servers  
\- concurrency primitives like channels, mutexes, and WaitGroups  
\- goroutines as you will use them to simulate the load on this broker

3\. Chat Application using WebSockets

Building a simple real-time chat application using WebSockets will help you understand

\- how WebSockets and persistent connections work  
\- how to store and retrieve data from databases

Doing these projects well will cover most of the Golang constructs and will help build a solid foundation to learn advanced topics.

⚡ I keep writing and sharing these engineering nuggets, so if you are keen on learning them, follow along.

arpitbhayani.me/courses

\#AsliEngineering \#Golang

Golang \- Best Resources 🎁

Golang is getting hugely popular 🚀

As we are specifically working in Golang for the past 7-8 years, we got a chance to explore Golang in depth. While experimenting with its best features we got our fair share of learning what works well and what doesn’t. 

Every day I get many messages from developers who are interested in learning Golang but don’t know what and how to learn. 

Following are resources if follow rigorously, you’ll get the best understanding of Golang which is most sought after by companies. 

✅ Basic Topics:-   
\- You can start with Go Tour, which is developed by the Go team itself, you can simply check and run the main features of Go online and don’t need to install Go locally.   
https://lnkd.in/dUd2kpKh

\- Topic wise Good collection of Go examples is good for understanding basic topics.   
https://gobyexample.com/

\- If you prefer learning through videos here’s a good course by Todd McLeod  
https://lnkd.in/dMM3M68A

\- Once you learn all the above things well   
Learn to create web-server using “net/http” package  
\- Create web-servers using Gin(so far the best router), learn middleware well.  
https://lnkd.in/dGprau3T  
\- Learn GORM first many companies are still using it, we prefer using SQLX for better performance.   
https://gorm.io/index.html  
https://lnkd.in/dqGjjW9F

\- Learn to create REST APIs with best practices, and develop CRUD APIs by connecting to relational DB (PostgreSQL/MySQL)

✅ Intermediate Topics:-   
\- Learn Interfaces well, empty interfaces, and type assertion, interface implementation.   
\- Advanced methods, struct composition   
\- Writing Unit tests 

✅ Advanced topics:-   
\- Goroutines, Channels, Wait Groups, these topics are a must we don’t hire Go, developers, if they don’t have a deep understanding of these concepts.   
\- Check the following superb video by Golang creator Rob Pike, he has explained “Concurrency is not Parallelism”  
https://lnkd.in/drWgE2ji

\- Concurrency patterns \- Worker Pool, Fan-In, Fan-Out, etc   
\- Mocking while writing Unit Tests (your knowledge of interfaces will be most important here)  
https://lnkd.in/dsRc\_d2V

\- Dependency injection, Wire is a superb library developed by the Google team  
https://lnkd.in/dQd3yMtU  
\- Pprof \- low-level CPU/Memory profiling 

I will keep updating this list

\=== POST 128 \===  
Bharat Khanna  
View Bharat Khanna’s profile  
   
• 1st  
Senior Software Engineer @Google | ex-Cohesity, TRC | ex-CTO @ PPA

2yr •   
2yr Visible to everyone

Solutions of Leetcode Weekly \#358

Problem 1: https://lnkd.in/d\_eKtWK6

Simple brute force to look at all pairs, find max digits in both numbers of the pair. If they are same, we can simply find the sum and check for max of all such sums. Remember to initialise your answer as \-1.

Time Complexity: O(n^2)  
Space Complexity: O(1)   
Solution Link: https://ideone.com/pqrMkK

Problem 2: https://lnkd.in/dXdcfZkN

Need to keep track of carry forward while multiplying the digits of linked list by 2 one by one.  
As the number is initially represented in reversed order, make sure to reverse the list first, then multiply by 2 and then reverse it back.

Time Complexity: O(n)  
Space Complexity: O(1) as same linked list was modified  
Solution Link: https://ideone.com/sKoy1A

Problem 3: https://lnkd.in/dieGhEbf

Sliding Window of fixed length based approach\! Initially all the elements can be kept into a multiset except those elements that come in the window of first element.  
Then when we move to next element, window moves forward. Relevant elements can be removed and added into the multiset. To calculate the answer, we just do lower bound on our multiset to find closest elements to our current element.

Make sure to handle the case where x, the length of the window range \= 0\.

Time Complexity: O(nlogn)  
Space Complexity: O(n)  
Solution Link: https://ideone.com/S0jU9N

Problem 4: https://lnkd.in/dJk-YnuP

Here, calculation of prime score for each element can be done via sieve based algorithm. Once we have the prime scores in place, each element would be the chosen one for those ranges where its prime score is maximum. 

To calculate this range, we can calculate the previous and next greater elements using stack based approach. 

Because when the prime scores are equal, we need to prefer the first element in the subarray, the calculation of previous Greater should infact be previous greater or equal.

Next, we can sort on the basis of their values (Since taking maximum values first will maximise the product).  
To handle multiplications, we also have to create a power function capable of taking mod with 1e9+7.

Time Complexity: O(nlogn)  
Space Complexity: O(n)  
Solution Link: https://ideone.com/7kEVim  
…see more

Account Login \- LeetCode

leetcode.com

\=== POST 129 \===  
Navneet Hingankar  
View Navneet Hingankar’s profile  
   
• 1st  
ex-Google | Founder AlgoScience | Master Codeforces

2yr •   
2yr Visible to everyone

todays leetcode intuition/solution:( a,b,c denotes the optimisation level, you can chose the one with shortest implementation)  
1\] n \= 100   
 a) clearly shouts use brute force and do what is said.   
 complexity O(n^2 \* L) , L represents length of number.   
 b) use array list of 10 elements where each list contains the element with their max value as \[0,10). now its just find two max elements from the individual list.

2\] double a number represented in linked list.  
 a) just use existing LC task, addition of two linked list and get done with it.(fastest)  
 b) use stack to handle addition.   
 c) its more like approach used in a) reverse the linked list. \<O(n), O(1)\>

3\] abs(i \- j) \>= x and minimize the absolute difference abs(nums\[i\] \- nums\[j\])  
 hint : in 99% of the task , wherever absolute is mentioned, just think of how to work on sorted something either index or elements. sorting can be achieved online/offline with as DS according to language you are using . but here, two conditions are mentioned, so how to deal with it, well imagine if we only put relevant indexes in set we can directly handle it.   
abs(i \- j) \>= x means work on only those elements whose, WLOG i \< j   
so j \- i \>= x , i \<= j \- x, i \< j \- x \+ 1, now when we increment j , j' \-\> j \+ 1  
 so now we got more possibilities for i' , i' \< j' \- x \+ 1, but not less. so we can add new i' satisfying the conditions, using incremental pointer.   
now the task is reduced to given a element y find closest element to it in the given multiset( as specified i am using multiset in c++) .   
CHALLENGE TO PROVE: Prove mathematically that we are covering all the possibilities or combinations of pairs. (hint: start small, still stuck start with smaller)   
OPT. in general we can use set here, but i think we can also use monotonic stack to reduce this to O(n) as it contains both sorted and relevant element, not sure tho.

4\] this is more of implementation task. first forget about this value of prime and all wasting candidates time, just assume it is normal array. whenever this is question work on array Y which derived from array X , as some function of X \-\>Y. i feel, its just redundant and confuses people more. plus it proves no point in the main logic of the task. so i will work only on array X.  
observe that we need to chose max from each segment with least index(least index is here just to fix the pivot), (another way to make task more complex is to derive the pivot based on some function of values LOL) .   
so we will prefer max it means fix max and find all the subarray that are intersecting or containing the element , leftmost as according to given condition. for this first you have to sort the array. lets say the index of this Mi   
so all the Li \<= Mi and Ri \>= Mi , \[Li, Ri\] will contain this as max value. rest everything is now with the same max value there will another index Mj , WLOG assume Mj \> Mi , so all the index Lj \<= Mj and Rj \>= Mj , \[Lj, Rj\] ,

The Top 8 API Architectural Styles You Should Know in 2023

REST (Representational State Transfer): A champion of simplicity and ubiquity, REST is an architectural style that primarily leverages HTTP methods. It enables easy interaction with resources, making it a go-to pattern for a multitude of applications and modern APIs.

SOAP (Simple Object Access Protocol): SOAP, a heavyweight contender in the API arena, thrives on complexity and power. It employs XML for defining structured communication. Although requiring a SOAP client and server, it compensates with its strength and robustness, much like a well-built off-road vehicle tackling rugged terrains.

GraphQL: A rising star in the API cosmos, GraphQL offers flexibility and precision. It lets clients ask for exactly what they need, reducing redundancy, and improving performance. Think of it as a personal shopper \- you get just what you asked for, nothing more, nothing less.

gRPC (Google Remote Procedure Call): gRPC is the speedster of the API universe. Running on HTTP/2 and using binary data, it's all about performance and speed, especially for microservices architectures. It's like a high-speed train, ensuring quick and reliable communication.

WebSockets: If real-time and bi-directional communication is what you need, WebSockets are the answer. Ideal for chat applications, live streaming, and real-time data exchange, it's like having an open telephone line between clients and servers.

Webhooks: Webhooks are the town criers of the digital world. They notify clients when certain server-side events occur, making them perfect for event-driven architectures. Imagine them as your personal alert system, keeping you informed of what matters.

MQTT (Message Queuing Telemetry Transport): MQTT is a lightweight messenger, designed specifically for environments with limited resources, low bandwidth, and unreliable networks. Picture it as a postal worker determined to deliver your mail, come rain or shine.

AMQP (Advanced Message Queuing Protocol): A robust and standardized protocol, AMQP excels in middleware environments with its reliable messaging capabilities. It's like a well-oiled assembly line, efficiently moving messages where they need to go.

Which API architectural style should you use?

The best API architectural style for a particular application will depend on the specific requirements of the application, such as \-

1\. The type of data that will be exchanged between the API and the client  
   
2\. The performance requirements of the API  
   
3\. The security requirements of the API  
   
4\. The scalability requirements of the API

Once you have considered these factors, you can start to narrow down your choices and choose the API architectural style that is best suited for your application.

What makes your resume not get shortlisted in Google ? 

Resume is not the description of what you are responsible for but rather what you accomplished 

For example a PM is responsible for creating roadmap , aligning stakeholders , drafting requirements etc . 

What is wrong?  
The problem is EVERY product manager is responsible for creating roadmap , aligning stakeholders , drafting requirements etc. 

What one should do ?   
Mention what impact you had , which can be written by the formula shared by Diego Granados "Accomplished \[X\] as measured by \[Y\] by doing \[Z\]" 

For Example   
Accomplished \[X\]: “Launched a communications platform”  
Measured by \[Y\]: “Reduced communication cost by 20%”  
By doing \[Z\]: “, by introducing new communication channels like Whatsapp and introducing capabilities to switch between messaging platforms”

Congratulations, you just got referred\! 🎉

A message that a lot of people want in their mailbox, isnt it?

But, leave referral, a lot of them don't even get a revert back of the message\! 

Why? 

Because their way of approaching is wrong ❌

Sending below phrases guarantees you dont get a revert back ever ⬇️

❌ "Hi Sir"  
❌ "Hi can you please refer me for java role?"  
❌ "Hi, is your company hiring?"  
❌ "Hi, is there any opening for someone with 2 year experience?"

So, NEVER send the above phrases while asking for a referral\! 🙌🏻

Then, what should you send? Read below 👇🏻

Here's a template you can use while sending a referral message:

Hi {Name of referee},

Hope you are good and doing well. 

I am {Your name} currently a final year student at {College name}, i am looking out for full time opportunities and luckily found a job opening in your organisation {XYZ Company} which matches my expertise and interest. The job link for the same is \- {Job link from careers page}. I would be more than happy if you could refer me for the same.

Here's why i think i am a good fit for the job role:

✅ Github/Portfolio/Project link  
✅ Leetcode/Codechef/Codeforces ratings and profile link   
✅ Codejam/Google Kickstart contest rankings  
✅ Any other relevant achievement

Attaching my resume below for reference.

Thank you,  
{Your name}

\=== POST 138 \===  
Bharat Khanna  
View Bharat Khanna’s profile  
   
• 1st  
Senior Software Engineer @Google | ex-Cohesity, TRC | ex-CTO @ PPA

2yr •   
2yr Visible to everyone

Solutions of today's Leetcode Contest (Weekly 357\)

Problem 1: Simple simulation problem. If you get a character 'i' reverse the string created so far. Otherwise, append the character.

Time Complexity: O(n^2)  
Space Complexity: O(n)  
Solution Link: https://ideone.com/bsVVTY  
Time and Space can be optimised by not creating a new string/by just noting the number of reversals. But, seemed unnecessary considering it was the first problem.

Problem 2: If any 2 adjacent elements summed to a value more than m, it was always possible to keep them together and remove other elements one by one. So, we just had to check if any two adjacent have sum \> m to get true.

Time Complexity: O(n)  
Space Complexity: O(1)  
Solution Link: https://ideone.com/l2M9ja  
Note: Just make sure to handle the corner cases of n=1 and n=2 well. 

Problem 3: First we need to use simultaneous BFS to find the closest 1 to each 0 (A Common Graph Problem).   
Once we had the distances in place, problem was reduced to finding the maximum minimum from the path. This max-mini pattern always indicates Binary Search on Answer technique.   
To prove it, we can see monotonicity too \- That is, if for some max value x, there exists a path from (0,0) to (n-1,m-1), then it exists for all values more than x too.

Time Complexity: O(n\*m\*log(n+m))  
Space Complexity: O(n\*m)  
Solution Link: https://ideone.com/HtdKz2

Problem 4: If there were no categories, it would have been a simple problem to sort and take top k from it.  
With introduction of categories, we might get a better answer by taking more elements from distinct categories.  
So, we start with top k without categories and calculate the amount. Now, each time, we try to add a new category replacing an older element from existing categories making sure we don't make a category extinct.

Time Complexity: O(NlogN)  
Space Complexity: O(k)  
Solution Link: https://ideone.com/z4uTQ0  
…see more

Meet Gorilla 🦍 : The Language Model That Can Interact with Over 1,600 APIs and Outperforms GPT-4 for API calls

Gorilla is an open-source project, created by Shishir Patil, a PhD Student in ML systems at UC Berkeley. 

It’s based on Falcon and MPT, two powerful language models that have been fine-tuned for API integration and usage. 

Gorilla can parse the Abstract Syntax Tree (AST) when writing code, resulting in semantically and syntactically correct API invocations. This means that it can significantly reduce hallucinations and incorrect syntax, which are common problems for other language models, such as GPT-4.

Some use cases for Gorilla are:

✅ Developing applications that require natural language interface to APIs, such as voice assistants, chatbots, or code editors.  
✅ Exploring and learning various APIs without having to read the documentation or write the code manually.  
✅ Generating code snippets or examples for documentation or tutorials using natural language queries.  
✅ Testing and debugging APIs by invoking them with different inputs and outputs using natural language queries.  
✅ Creating innovative and functional applications that leverage the power of large language models and a wide range of APIs.

Gorilla is also compatible with commercial use, allowing developers to incorporate it into their projects without any obligations.

It’s available for use in various environments, including Google Colab and Command Line Interface (CLI) through pip installation of “gorilla-cli.” 

Gorilla also comes with APIBench, a curated collection of APIs that facilitates easy training and expands the available resources for Gorilla to call upon. API developers are also welcome to join the cause and contribute their APIs for inclusion in the ever-growing API store.

Gorilla is a game-changer in the domain of API integration and usage. It can help developers save time and effort, as well as create more innovative and functional applications. It can also help language model enthusiasts explore the potential of large language models for practical purposes.

And don’t forget to share this post with your network, so more people can discover Gorilla and its amazing capabilities.

The link to Gorrila in the first comment 👇

ChatGPT is a free Job search Specialist But 99% of people have no idea how to use it for job search.

Check and Save these \- 5 powerful prompts to accelerate your job search\! 

1\. Prompt for Resume Review.

"I want you to act as a skilled resume reviewer and evaluate my resume to help me achieve my career goals. Provide comprehensive feedback on the overall format, layout, and design of my resume to ensure it is visually appealing and professional. Analyze the content of each section, including the summary, work experience, education, and skills, and offer valuable suggestions to highlight my key achievements and contributions effectively. Additionally, assess the use of keywords and industry-specific terminology to tailor my resume for specific job opportunities.

\[Copy-Paste\] \- Resume 

2\. Prompt for Linkedin review

"I want you to act as a professional LinkedIn expert and conduct a thorough review of my LinkedIn profile. Offer valuable feedback on my profile picture, headline, and summary to ensure they present a strong and compelling personal brand. Analyze the consistency and relevance of my work experience, education, and skills sections, and suggest improvements to showcase my professional achievements and expertise better.” 

\[Copy-Paste\] \- Linkedin Profile after downloading it in pdf \- Don't add the link

3\. Interview Preparation and questions

"I want you to act as an interview preparation coach and equip me with the skills and knowledge to ace my upcoming interviews. Based on the \[Your industry and job role You are targeting\], create a customized list of common interview questions I am likely to encounter. Help me craft thoughtful and compelling answers that showcase my qualifications and experience effectively.

4\. Write a prompt for Company research for the Interview.

“Act as my company research guide to help me prepare for an upcoming interview. Conduct in-depth research on its background, culture, and values by understanding the company's mission and vision to gain insights into its overall objectives and goals. Investigate their products or services, target market, and competitive position within the industry.  
Prepare a list of thoughtful questions to ask during the interview to demonstrate my knowledge and genuine interest in the company.”

Company Name: XYZ

Sharing some super-useful resources for 𝗯𝗹𝗼𝗴𝘀 𝗳𝗼𝗿 𝗹𝗲𝗮𝗿𝗻𝗶𝗻𝗴 𝗗𝗦𝗔 𝗮𝗻𝗱 𝗖𝗼𝗺𝗽𝗲𝘁𝗶𝘁𝗶𝘃𝗲 𝗣𝗿𝗼𝗴𝗿𝗮𝗺𝗺𝗶𝗻𝗴.  
I have learned a lot of things from many of these personally.

1\) cp-algorithms \- Arguably the best blogs-site on the internet for CP. It is an ongoing translation project, new blogs are being added but most major ones are already present.

2\) codeforces/catalog \- Catalog of all the amazing blogs written on Codeforces.

3\) geeksforgeeks/fundamentals-algorithms \- This one is probably one of the most well-known ones.

4\) hackerearth/codemonk \- Hackerearth CodeMonk is not that well-known relatively. But it's a good starting point for beginners.

In the end, some additional thoughts \- Competitive programming is a hard skill (as in soft/hard skills). To learn any hard skill, you need practice and lots of it. Organized plans can help in improving faster. But still, you will need lots of practice, be very clear about that.

Especially If you're a newbie, don't wait for the perfect plan to come up or look at 10s of plans to start. Start right away, in the beginning, that's the most important thing.

P.S \- All full links in the comment.

2yr •   
2yr Visible to everyone

Tries are an important data structure with many real-world applications.

Here are 8 types of problems and patterns where you can use them (with Leetcode problem links):

1\) Prefix Matching: Tries are very efficient at finding all words with a common prefix.  
Problem: https://lnkd.in/gimNNq56

2\) Dictionary Implementations: Tries are ideal for implementing dictionary-like data structures for fast word retrieval.  
Problem: https://lnkd.in/gAH5a-7M

3\) Word Frequency: Tries can help in counting the frequency of words in a large text or document.  
Problem: https://lnkd.in/gUWi2r86

4\) Pattern Matching: Tries can be used to find patterns quickly and efficiently. They are used heavily to process DNA sequences and other biological data.  
Problem: https://lnkd.in/g9rPaym9

5\) Lexicographic Sorting: Tries can efficiently sort strings lexicographically.  
Problem: https://lnkd.in/gFM33dQJ

6\) Auto-complete and Search Suggestion: Tries can be efficiently used to suggest word completions and auto-complete. A popular feature on search engines.  
Problem: https://lnkd.in/g-TXKjaB

7\) Longest Prefix Matching: They can be used for finding the longest prefix match in a set of string.  
Problem: https://lnkd.in/gMKrghkz

8\) Word Games: Tries are used in games like Scrabble or Boggle for word validation.  
Problem: https://lnkd.in/geXH9tc3

\=== POST 149 \===  
Ali Abdaal  
View Ali Abdaal’s profile  
   
• 2nd  
👨‍⚕️ Doctor-turned-Entrepreneur \+ Productivity Expert \+ YouTuber (6M subs) 📘 New York Times Bestselling Author of "Feel-Good Productivity"

2yr •   
2yr Visible to everyone

I’ve read close to 1000 books.

I’ve narrowed it down to 15 books everyone needs to read (2023):

1\. The Pathless Path.

This book is great for you if you’re unsure of what you want to do in life.

2\. Someday is Today.

This book is great for you if you have dreams of starting your own business or a new venture but you’ve been waiting for the right time.

3\. Beyond Wealth.

This book is great because the author Alexander Green has worked with a lot of wealthy people & found that money itself doesn’t make you happy.

4\. The 3 Alarms.

3 pieces of advice I loved:

1\. The 3 alarms method, which helps remind you of the identity you want to have  
2\. The ideal week, which I’ve been using for the last few months  
3\. The weekly review, where you review how your week went at the end of each week

5\. The Art and Business of Online Writing.

The author Nicholas Cole talks about how he went from playing World of Warcraft to finding online writing, which has made him super successful.

6\. The 7 Habits of Highly Effective People.

This is one of the best self-help/ productivity book I’ve ever read.

7\. Scorecard Marketing.

This book is only useful if you want to start a business or are currently running one.

It’s taught me a lot about marketing & more importantly, the scorecard method, which I’ve started using in my business.

8\. What We Owe The Future.

Someone described this book as a textbook for philosophy mixed with a pamphlet for activism & I completely agree with that statement.

9\. The Go Giver.

This book is a business fable & teaches you how to be more giving in life rather than transactional.

10\. The Luck Factor.

It covers four main things lucky people do that unlucky people don’t.

11\. The Way of The Superior Man.

It’s a little controversial but an interesting read.

I think anyone who reads it would find it interesting regardless of their views.

12\. $100m Offers.

This is a required read if you’re starting a business or already running one.

10 people recommended me this book & it did not disappoint.

13\. Sapiens. 

This book is a brief look at the history of humankind.

I started reading it because I wanted to get more into history & I quickly understood why everyone was talking about it.

14\. The Surrender Experiment.

This book follows the journey of a guy who decided at 21 he would surrender to the experiment of life & get heavily into spirituality/ yoga. 

He ended up becoming the CEO of a $1 billion medical company through his journey.

15\. The Seven Husbands of Evelyn Hugo.

It follows the journey of Evelyn Hugo, who was an actress in the 1940s & talks about all of the things she had to deal with in Hollywood as a woman.

Bonus books. The Stormlight Archive.

These are my favourite fiction books next to Harry Potter.

The author does a great job of building the universe in these books.

Definitely check it out if you’re into books like Harry Potter & other fiction series.

What other books should I read? :)  
…see more
